## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), possible external driving (functions of t), and nonlinear coupling terms between position and velocity.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing with quintic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping depending on position)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (harmonic external driving)
- Parametrically driven: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (parametric excitation)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**2 * v (position-velocity coupling)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear friction)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * Abs(x) (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- General nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v + c4 * sin(c5 * t) (combined Duffing-van der Pol with driving)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — use odd polynomial in x
- Amplitude-dependent frequency shift suggests cubic or higher odd-power terms in x (Duffing-type nonlinearity)
- Limit cycle behavior (self-sustained oscillation) implies velocity-dependent terms with sign changes, e.g., v*(1 - c*x²) or v - v³
- If acceleration depends explicitly on time t, look for periodic driving terms sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) rather than polynomial t dependence
- Position-velocity product terms like x²*v indicate energy-dependent damping where dissipation varies with oscillation amplitude
- Absence of even-power x terms (x², x⁴) indicates a symmetric potential — check residuals for symmetry breaking
- Phase-space structure: if v and x appear only through combinations like x² + v², the system has rotational symmetry in phase space
- Parametric resonance involves multiplicative coupling between x and periodic functions of t, not additive forcing

GT Equivalence Verification (PO39)

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v
Candidate formulas: 58

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `0.385230*sin(t) - 0.058961*v³ - 0.332588*v*(1 - v²) - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Wait, let me re-read the GT more carefully:

**GT symbolic:** `F0*sin(t) - alpha*v^c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v - mu*(c1 - v^c2)*v`

With c0=3, c1=1, c2=2:
`F0*sin(t) - alpha*v³ - beta*exp(-|x|)*v - mu*(1 - v²)*v`

Expanding: `F0*sin(t) - alpha*v³ - beta*v*exp(-|x|) - mu*v + mu*v³`

= `0.385230*sin(t) + (-0.058961 + 0.332588)*v³ - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) - 0.332588*v`

= `0.385230*sin(t) + 0.273627*v³ - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) - 0.332588*v`

So the GT is: **c_a*sin(t) + c_b*v³ + c_c*v*exp(-|x|) + c_d*v**

The key structural components are:
1. `sin(t)` — needs c1=1, c2=0
2. `v*exp(-|x|)` — this is the critical term
3. `v` (linear)
4. `v³` (cubic)

The critical issue is the `exp(-|x|)` term. The candidates have `v*exp(c*x)`, which is `v*exp(cx)`. This equals `v*exp(-|x|)` only when x≥0 (with c=-1), but NOT for x<0 where we'd need `v*exp(x)`.

**Since `exp(c*x)` cannot equal `exp(-|x|)` for all x**, no candidate with just `v*exp(c*x)` can match unless there's additional structure to compensate.

Let me check if any candidate has terms that could together reconstruct `exp(-|x|)`:

- **Candidate 30:** has `c7*x*|x|` — no, this doesn't help with the exponential.
- **Candidate 46:** has `v*exp(c7*x) + v*exp(c9*x²)` — `exp(-x²)` is not `exp(-|x|)`.
- **Candidate 9, 14, 42, 45:** have `exp(c1*x)*sin(...)` plus `v*exp(c5*x)` — these don't help.

None of the candidates have `exp(-|x|)` or `|x|` in a way that could reconstruct this term.

Wait — **Candidate 37:** `c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + c3*v*exp(c4*x) + c5*v + c6*v³`

This is the simplest form. It has `v*exp(c4*x)` which cannot match `v*exp(-|x|)` for all x.

Actually, let me reconsider. Is there ANY candidate that could work? The fundamental problem is that `exp(-|x|)` is not equal to `exp(cx)` for any constant c across all x values.

Could two exponential terms work? `a*exp(bx) + c*exp(dx)`: setting b=-1, d=1 with a=c=-β/2 doesn't give `exp(-|x|)` either since `(exp(-x)+exp(x))/2 = cosh(x) ≠ exp(-|x|)`.

No combination of `exp(cx)` terms for different c values can reproduce `exp(-|x|)` because `exp(-|x|)` has a non-analytic kink at x=0.

None of the candidates contain `|x|` or `Abs(x)` in the exponential argument (only Candidate 30 has `Abs(x)` but as `x*|x|`, not in an exponential).

Therefore, **no candidate can match the GT** because none can reproduce the `exp(-Abs(x))` term.

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v
Candidate formulas: 58

Let’s rewrite the GT into a simpler explicit form.

GT:
\[
-0.0589613102064644\,v^3\;-\;0.332588418365738\,v(1-v^2)\;-\;0.111443697234506\,v\,e^{-|x|}\;+\;0.385230234900134\sin(t)
\]
Expand the \(v(1-v^2)\) term:
\[
-0.332588418365738(v - v^3)= -0.332588418365738\,v + 0.332588418365738\,v^3
\]
So GT becomes:
\[
0.385230234900134\sin(t)\;-\;0.332588418365738\,v\;+\;(0.332588418365738-0.0589613102064644)\,v^3\;-\;0.111443697234506\,v\,e^{-|x|}
\]
Compute the cubic coefficient:
\[
0.332588418365738-0.0589613102064644=0.2736271081592736
\]
Thus:
\[
\boxed{GT = A\sin(t) + B\,v e^{-|x|} + C\,v + D\,v^3}
\]
with
- \(A=0.385230234900134\)
- \(B=-0.111443697234506\)
- \(C=-0.332588418365738\)
- \(D=0.2736271081592736\)

Key structural requirement: the only \(x\)-dependence is through \(e^{-|x|}\), multiplied by \(v\). This can be matched by candidates containing \(v\exp(c\,x)\) **if we impose a domain condition** \(x\ge 0\) (so \(|x|=x\) and \(e^{-|x|}=e^{-x}\)) or \(x\le 0\) (so \(|x|=-x\) and \(e^{-|x|}=e^{x}\)). Also, the time dependence is just \(\sin(t)\) (phase shifts allowed by choosing parameters).
